The sensation for the user is expansion: the boundary of self extends past the skin, and the user feels the field the way they feel their own body — as territory, as owned space. Touching a Paramount's field without invitation is, on a proprioceptive level, touching them. They feel it. They react.

Vassago Moren's Bastioning — his Conqueror-tier Armoring that manifests as layered tectonic plates — is reported to generate a field so dense that standing within arm's reach produces a sensation of atmospheric pressure, as if the altitude has dropped a thousand feet. His crew has adapted. Outsiders have not. A visiting captain who shook Vassago's hand described the experience as "shaking hands with a building that was also somehow a person."

**When Armoring Breaks**

The sensation of Armoring cracking under sufficient force is universally described as the worst pain in Dominion use. Not because of the physical damage — though that follows — but because of the violation. Armoring is will made physical. When it breaks, the user feels their will break. The sensation is not a crack but a collapse — a sudden, total loss of the barrier between self and world, accompanied by a rush of sensation that the Armoring had been filtering: every sound louder, every surface sharper, every nerve firing at full reception after being muted. Users who have survived Armoring failure describe a moment of nakedness that is not physical but existential — the sudden awareness that the thing they believed would protect them has been overcome, and the world is closer and more dangerous than they remembered.

Recovery from Armoring failure takes days to weeks. The sheen returns in patches — unreliable, flickering, the user's confidence rebuilding unevenly across the body. The last place Armoring returns is wherever it broke. A user whose chest-plate was shattered will find their chest the last area to re-Armor, sometimes weeks after the rest of the body has recovered. The body remembers where the will failed, and the memory resists.

---

#### B. What Vision Feels Like From Inside

**Tempered**

The first time Vision activates — often spontaneously, often during adolescence, often during a moment of fear or intense focus — the world opens. Not visually. The eyes don't change. What changes is the space behind the eyes — a sudden expansion of awareness that processes information the eyes were never designed to collect. A Tempered Vision user describes it as "the room getting bigger." Not physically — perceptually. The walls are still where they were. But the user can feel them without looking. The person standing behind them has a heartbeat that registers as a faint pressure in the Vision user's awareness, a rhythmic pulse that says: alive, standing, nervous.

The nervous part is the problem. Vision at Tempered level is crude — it reads presence, not intent. The user knows someone is behind them but not whether that person is a threat, a friend, or a stranger looking for the bathroom. The resolution is low. The experience is overwhelming. A Tempered Vision user in a crowded market feels every person in the space as a separate signal — heartbeats, body heat, movement patterns — and the signals merge into a noise that produces headaches, nausea, and the specific sensory exhaustion that Vision trainees call "the flood." Learning to use Vision is not learning to see more. It is learning to ignore most of what you see.

Khari, with their enhanced biological senses, have an easier transition — their nervous systems are already processing environmental data at a higher baseline, and Vision augments existing channels rather than opening new ones. A canine Khari whose scent-processing is already superhuman experiences Vision as an extension of smell into intent: the person behind them doesn't just have a heartbeat — they smell anxious. The biological and Dominion senses blend, and the result is a perceptive resolution that pure-Vision users take decades to match.

**Forged**

At Forged level, the noise resolves. Vision becomes selective — the user can focus on one signal in a crowd, isolating a specific heartbeat from the background the way a trained ear isolates a single voice in a chorus. The headaches stop. The nausea stops. What replaces them is a quieter, more unsettling experience: clarity.

A Forged Vision user reading a person's heartbeat can feel the skip that means the person is lying. Not interpret — feel. The lie registers as a hiccup in the signal, a stutter in the rhythm that is as obvious to the Vision user as a flinch is to the eye. The user is not reading minds. They are reading bodies at a resolution that makes deception functionally transparent. Forged Vision users report that social interaction changes permanently at this level — not because they choose to read people, but because they cannot stop. A Forged Vision user at dinner with friends is, at all times, aware of who is uncomfortable, who is attracted to whom, who drank too much, and who is pretending to laugh. The awareness is not voluntary. It is the baseline.

This is where Vision becomes a burden. A Tempered user can turn it off — the skill is new, conscious, and deactivates when attention drifts. A Forged user's Vision is always partially on, the way a Forged Armoring user always has a passive sheen. The world is always transparent, always readable, and the user must develop not the skill to perceive but the discipline to not act on what they perceive. A Forged Vision user who mentions, casually, that their dinner companion is attracted to the server — because the heartbeat said so, because the pupils said so, because the body's language was louder than the mouth's — has violated a social contract that the rest of the table didn't know was being monitored. The loneliness of high-level Vision users is documented. The information isolates. Knowing what everyone feels makes it harder to feel with them, because the mystery that sustains intimacy — the not-knowing, the wondering, the vulnerability of guessing — is gone. A Vision user who can read their partner's heart in real time has lost the ability to be surprised by it.

**Paramount**

At Paramount level, Vision extends across distances that break the metaphor of "sight." A Paramount Vision user perceives across miles — not visual data but structural data, the shape of intent and movement patterns at a scale that is more like weather prediction than perception. Dalverre Koss, the Wardensea Paramount, is documented tracking a fleeing ship by the crew's collective emotional state from seven miles away. She describes the experience as "reading a current" — the ship's movement, the crew's anxiety, the captain's decision to flee, all registering as a single flowing signal that she follows the way a Khari follows a scent trail.

Reading intent at Paramount level is no longer body-reading. It is predictive modeling done in real time by a nervous system that has been processing Dominion data for decades. The user feels what the target is going to do before the target has committed to doing it. The lead time is one to three seconds for humans, up to ten for Lunarians (whose Silverborn-descended nervous systems process Vision at a different speed). The sensation is not premonition — it is recognition. The user has seen enough patterns, at enough resolution, that the next movement in the pattern is obvious the way the next word in a familiar sentence is obvious. A Paramount Vision user in combat is, functionally, fighting someone whose actions are arriving in slow motion — not because time has changed but because the Vision user has already read the commitment before the body executes it.

**The Thing Vision Users Wish They Didn't Know**

Vision users in crowded spaces see things they cannot unsee. The man across the market whose heartbeat spikes when he looks at children — the Vision user feels the spike, reads the arousal, and cannot unknow it. The woman at the next table whose body is in pain — not injury-pain but the sustained, chronic pain of illness that she hasn't told anyone about, and the Vision user feels it as a persistent ache in their own awareness. The couple who are performing happiness while their heartbeats tell a completely different story.

High-level Vision users develop a specific emotional callus — not indifference but triage. They learn to prioritize which signals to attend to and which to let pass through without engagement. The alternative is drowning in other people's truth. The Collegium Verossian's Applied Dominion department has documented cases of Vision users who could not develop this callus and were eventually overwhelmed — unable to enter crowded spaces, unable to sustain relationships, unable to distinguish their own emotional state from the emotional signals surrounding them. The condition is called **"the Glass"** — the Vision user becomes transparent to everything and opaque to themselves. It is rare. It is incurable. It is the price of a gift that was designed by a god of memory, and memory, as Hettashi knows, does not forget.

---

#### C. What King Feels Like — From Both Sides

**Projecting King**

King does not feel like power. Every user who has attempted to describe it reaches for that word first and discards it. Power implies control. King, especially in its early manifestations, is not controlled — it is released.

The first King manifestation is usually accidental, usually emotional, and usually catastrophic. The user feels a pressure building in the chest — not physical pressure but existential pressure, the sensation of something inside them that is too large for the space it occupies and is demanding, with increasing urgency, to be expressed. The pressure is tied to conviction — the stronger the user's feelings about the situation, the greater the pressure — and the release, when it comes, is not a decision. It is a rupture. The will goes outward. The people around the user go down.

Thessan Mulvarri's first manifestation — age sixteen, festival brawl, forty-seven people unconscious including his foster family — is the textbook example. He describes the moment before the release as "drowning on land." The world was too close, the conflict too present, and something in him responded by pushing everything away. The push was King. The forty-seven people on the ground were the consequence. The silence afterward — forty-seven bodies down, the festival noise stopped, Thessan standing in the center of a circle of unconscious people and understanding, for the first time, what he was — is the silence that every King user remembers from their first manifestation. The silence is not calm. It is the sound of having done something you cannot take back.

At trained levels, King becomes more deliberate but never fully controlled. A Forged King user can direct the output — aiming it at a group, narrowing it to a section of a room — but the generation of King remains emotional rather than mechanical. You cannot King someone you don't care about. The output requires conviction, and conviction is not a switch. A King user who is tired, depressed, grieving, or morally uncertain generates measurably less output. The First Law of Dominion — conviction amplifies, doubt suppresses — is felt by King users as a direct correlation between emotional state and capability. A King user who has lost faith in their cause is a King user who cannot project, and the inability to project when you know you should be able to is described as "reaching for a hand that isn't there."

What projecting King feels like at sustained output: exhaustion that begins in the center of the chest and radiates. Not muscular fatigue — existential fatigue, as if the user is spending themselves, converting identity into force. A Conqueror who deploys King at full output for extended periods reports feeling "thinner" — less present, less substantial, as if the will being projected outward is being subtracted from the self. Garra Vassun Thane, holding King continuously for twenty-two years in the Vorrenmaw, is consuming himself in the most literal sense the metaphor allows. His body is failing because his will has been deployed outside his body for two decades, and the body without the full presence of the will deteriorates the way a house deteriorates without maintenance.

**Receiving King**

The experience of being hit by King depends on the tier of the projector and the resistance of the target. At every level, the first sensation is the same: wrongness. Something is in the room that wasn't there before — a pressure, a presence, a weight that has no physical source. The air hasn't changed. The temperature hasn't changed. But something fundamental about the space has shifted, and the body knows it before the mind does. The hair stands. The stomach drops. The hindbrain — the ancient, pre-rational part of the nervous system — fires a signal that translates roughly as: you have made a terrible mistake by being here.

**From a Tempered King user:** The sensation is intimidation. Not the social kind — the biological kind. The body wants to leave. The legs want to back up. The eyes want to look away. The target can resist, because the output at Tempered level is broad and unfocused, more atmosphere than assault. But the resistance costs effort, and the effort compounds — five minutes in a room with a Tempered King user who is projecting is five minutes of sustained psychological resistance that leaves the target tired, anxious, and unable to articulate why.

**From a Forged King user:** The intimidation becomes physical. The pressure is no longer atmosphere — it is weight. Targets describe it as a hand pressing down on the top of the skull, or as a sudden increase in gravity localized to their body. Breathing becomes conscious. Standing becomes effortful. Weaker targets — those with no Armoring, no King resistance, no Korvaan training — lose consciousness. Not from impact. From submission. The body decides, below the level of conscious choice, that resistance is not survivable, and shuts down. The unconsciousness is not painful. It is, by most accounts, almost peaceful — a sudden release of the effort of standing up against something that outweighs you. Waking up is worse. The shame of having been dropped by someone else's will — of knowing that your body surrendered without your permission — is the part that stays.

**From a Paramount King user:** Selectivity. The horror of Paramount-tier King is not its strength but its precision. Banzan can drop every Tempered fighter in a stadium and leave the civilians standing. The civilians feel the King as a pressure, a headache, a sense that something terrible is happening nearby. The fighters feel the King as a targeted, personal assault — the weight lands on them specifically, finds the frequency of their will and overrides it. The experience is described as "being erased" — not killed, not hurt, but temporarily removed from the equation of the room. Your will is not strong enough. The Paramount's will is. The math is simple and absolute and you are the smaller number.

**From a Conqueror King user:** At Conqueror level, King is no longer pressure. It is weather. Vassago Moren's King has literal atmospheric weight — standing near him when he projects changes the pressure in the room enough to pop ears. Kuorren Vasseg's King is different — it doesn't crush, it persuades. Targets don't faint; they agree. They find themselves nodding, stepping aside, lowering weapons, not because they've been forced but because, for the duration of the projection, Kuorren's perspective seems obviously correct. The experience of being Kuorren'd — the term his enemies coined — is worse than being dropped, because you remember agreeing and you remember meaning it, and the residue of artificial conviction lingers for hours, making the target question every opinion they hold. "If he could make me believe that, what else do I believe that isn't mine?"

Senmovar's King is silent. That is the word every target uses. Not quiet — silent. There is no pressure. There is no weight. There is simply a moment where you were conscious and then a moment where you were not, and the gap between contains nothing. Targets who have survived Senmovar's King describe waking up with the sensation that time was stolen — not lost, stolen, removed by someone who took it without asking and left no mark. Two hundred and forty-one years of refinement has produced a King so controlled that its exercise is, from the target's perspective, indistinguishable from non-existence.

---

#### D. The Social Reality of Dominion

Dominion is not separate from daily life. It is daily life, the way gravity is daily life — pervasive, invisible when unremarkable, and impossible to ignore when it isn't.

A Tempered shopkeeper in Thalveris doesn't consciously Armor when a customer gets aggressive. But the faint sheen appears on the hands, the jaw tightens, and the customer — if they have any Vision sensitivity at all — feels the shift and recalibrates. The negotiation changes. The customer is not aware why they've suddenly become more polite. The shopkeeper is not aware they've projected. The exchange completes, both parties walk away, and Dominion has shaped a commercial interaction that neither participant would describe as involving supernatural force. This happens ten thousand times a day across the world. This is what Dominion looks like at ground level.

A Forged parent intimidates their child's teacher by accident. The parent walks into the school building for a routine meeting, and the teacher — Tempered at best, more likely Flickering — feels the parent's passive Armoring field as a pressure in the room. The air changes. The teacher's posture shifts, becomes more deferential. The parent notices and is mortified. They have come to discuss their daughter's reading level, and the teacher is responding to them as if they've come to discuss the teacher's continued employment. The parent drops their Armoring consciously, which takes effort and makes them feel exposed, and the meeting proceeds normally, except the teacher will always, slightly, flinch when this parent's name comes up. This is the social reality of Dominion disparity: the strong must constantly monitor themselves around the weak, and the weak must constantly manage their reactions to the strong, and the effort of this mutual management is exhausting and invisible and never discussed.

People move differently around someone who's visibly Armored. A Forged Wardensea officer walking through a market in full sheen creates a wake — pedestrians step wider, conversations pause and resume, eye contact is offered and immediately broken. The officer may be buying vegetables. The sheen may be passive, unconscious, the default state of a body that has been Armored for twenty years. The market responds anyway. Dominion hierarchy is felt in the body before it's processed by the mind, and the body's response — defer, avoid, create space — is not choice. It is instinct, and the instinct is correct, because the sheen means this person can hurt you in ways you cannot reciprocate, and the body knows this before the conscious mind has finished assessing the officer's shopping list.

**Dating with Vision:** The experience of a Vision user on a date is the experience of a person who has been given the answer key to a test they wanted to take honestly. A Forged Vision user sitting across from someone they're attracted to can read the attraction being returned — the elevated heartbeat, the dilated pupils, the specific pattern of blood flow that signals arousal. They know. They know before the other person has decided whether to express it. The temptation to act on the knowledge is constant. The ethics of acting on it are murky. Is it manipulation to touch someone's hand when you know they want you to? Is it dishonest to pretend surprise at a confession you heard coming in the heartbeat thirty seconds before the words arrived?

Vision users in relationships develop protocols. Some disclose their ability immediately — "I can read your body at a level you can't control, and I need you to know that." Some disclose gradually, as trust builds. Some never disclose, and the relationship proceeds with one partner seeing through walls the other doesn't know are transparent. The ethics vary by culture: the Morventhi, who prize openness, consider non-disclosure of Vision a violation. The Thalessi, who prize privacy, consider unsolicited Vision-reading an invasion regardless of disclosure. The Khari, whose biological senses already cross the boundary between public and private (canine Khari can literally smell arousal), find the entire debate quaint.

**The Dominion Wealth Gap:** Dominion output correlates with training, talent, and resources. Training requires time. Time requires money. The best Dominion training in the world is at the Collegium Verossian in Tourrenne — tuition: 400 Gold Sovereigns per year. The second best is Wardensea boot camp — free, but you owe fifteen years of service. The result: the highest Dominion output in the civilian population correlates with wealth, and the highest in the military population correlates with institutional loyalty. A Rathai in the Nettleworks with raw King potential that equals Thessan Mulvarri's will never develop it, because the training costs more than her family earns in a decade and the Wardensea route means serving the institution that underfunds her home. The Masqarat does not suppress Dominion. It doesn't need to. The price of developing Dominion suppresses it for them.

---

#### E. Dominion Accidents and Embarrassments

Dominion goes wrong. The bible acknowledges surge-lock during intimacy. The lived reality is broader, messier, and frequently hilarious in retrospect and terrifying in the moment.

**Surge-Lock During Intimacy — Expanded**

The bible establishes that Armoring can involuntarily activate during sex. The experience: arousal triggers the same nervous system pathways that combat-readiness triggers, and in users whose Armoring training has not yet separated the two responses, the sheen activates at the worst possible moment. The skin hardens. The partner — who was, moments ago, touching something warm and yielding — is now touching something that feels like polished stone and is about as responsive. The user can feel the partner's hands on them but the sensation is muted, filtered through the sheen, and the intimacy is replaced by the specific horror of being trapped inside your own defense mechanism during the one moment you most want to be defenseless.

The partner's response depends on the partner. An experienced partner — someone who has been with Dominion users before — recognizes the sheen, stops, and waits. They know the surge-lock breaks when the panic subsides, and the panic subsides faster when nobody makes it worse. An inexperienced partner panics, which escalates the user's panic, which strengthens the sheen, which increases the panic, which — in documented cases — has produced a feedback loop that kept the user fully Armored for up to forty minutes while both parties sat on opposite sides of the bed trying to breathe.

Wardensea barracks humor about surge-lock is relentless. Every recruit hears the stories. The stories are exaggerated and the exaggeration is kind — it normalizes an experience that, for the user, is genuinely traumatic. A young Wardensea officer who surge-locks during their first sexual experience may never speak of it, but they will hear seventeen jokes about it in the mess hall that week, and the jokes tell them: this is common, this is survivable, and the person who tells the best joke about it probably has their own story they're not telling.

**Involuntary Armoring During Nightmares**

This happens. The user is asleep. The nightmare triggers a combat response. The sheen activates, and the user's body becomes a hardened surface while they thrash through the dream. The bed suffers. Wooden bed-frames crack. Mattresses compress under the localized weight increase. Partners who are sharing the bed wake to the sensation of lying next to something that has become, without warning, a stone. The bruises are distinctive — Armoring-contact bruises are deeper and more uniform than impact bruises, because the surface that caused them was smooth and impossibly hard.

Gorundai couples, who are statistically more likely to produce Armoring-heavy users, have a tradition of separate sleeping surfaces during the early years of Armoring training. The tradition is practical — a Gorundai at Tempered level who Armors in their sleep is heavy enough to crack a bed-frame and hard enough to break a partner's rib. The tradition is also the subject of a specific Gorundai joke: "You know the marriage is real when you survive the first night without furniture." The joke is told at weddings. The furniture replacement is budgeted.

**Vision Reading Something You Didn't Want to Know**

A Forged Vision user at a family dinner reads their parent's heartbeat and discovers — not through confession, not through evidence, but through the involuntary spike that occurs when the parent looks at a specific person — that the parent is having an affair. The Vision user did not ask for this information. The information is now permanent. The parent does not know the child knows. The child cannot unknow it. The dinner continues. The food tastes different.

A Vision user at a funeral reads the widow's heartbeat and discovers that the grief is real but the love was not. The widow is performing sorrow for a partner she stopped loving years ago, and the performance is flawless except for the heartbeat, which is steady and calm and tells a story the eulogy is contradicting. The Vision user stands at the back and says nothing and carries the knowledge home and adds it to the collection of truths they did not ask for that sits in their memory like stones in a pocket.

A Vision user in a crowded market reads a child's fear and follows it to the source: a parent whose heartbeat accelerates with anger when the child speaks. The Vision user sees the trajectory — the escalation pattern, the specific cardiac signature of someone about to lose control — and must decide, in real time, whether to intervene in a stranger's family based on data that no one else in the market can perceive. The decision is not simple. The data is unambiguous. The social contract has no protocol for "I can feel that you're about to hurt your child." The Vision user intervenes or doesn't, and either choice costs something.

**A Child's First King Manifestation**

The location is always wrong. A school. A family dinner. A birthday party. King manifests from conviction, and a child's convictions are enormous and unregulated — the fury of injustice, the desperation of fear, the absolute certainty that something is unfair and must be stopped. The child feels the pressure build in the chest and does not have the framework to understand what it is, and the release is uncontrolled, undirected, and devastating at close range.

A twelve-year-old human boy in a Thalveris school manifests King during a fight over a stolen toy. The teacher drops. Three classmates drop. The boy stands in the center of the room, terrified, surrounded by unconscious people and the specific silence that follows a King burst. He does not know what he did. He knows he did something. The remaining children — those too far away to be affected, or those with enough natural resistance to stay conscious — are staring at him with an expression he will remember for the rest of his life: the expression of people who have just learned what he is.

The parents are called. The Wardensea is called. The next three days determine the child's future: Wardensea recruitment pitch (free training, fifteen years of service, the institution gets a King user), family refusal (the child trains privately, at enormous cost, or doesn't train at all), or the third option that no one discusses in polite company — the family moves to a port city, changes the child's name, and hopes the Wardensea's records are as poorly organized as their reputation suggests.

Gorundai and Oni families handle first King manifestations differently. The Gorundai response is structured: the child is removed from the situation, assessed by the nearest Dominion-experienced elder, and given a framework — "what happened to you is called King, it comes from your will, and you will learn to direct it." The framework is calm, practical, and presented with the Gorundai conviction that any problem with a name is a problem that can be managed.

The Oni response is celebration. An Oni child who manifests King for the first time has demonstrated, in the most dramatic possible way, that they have the strength of will to impose themselves on the world. The child is terrified. The community is delighted. The disconnect between the child's panic and the adults' excitement is, for the child, deeply confusing, and the confusion resolves only when the child understands that in Oni culture, King is not a burden. It is a gift. The storm gave it. The mountain carries it. The child who can knock down a room full of adults is not dangerous — they are promising. The celebration, for non-Oni observers, is alarming. For the child, it is the first moment of a lifelong relationship with a power that their culture does not fear, and the absence of fear is, for an Oni King user, the foundation of everything that follows.

## 12. GOD FRUIT SYSTEM — Complete Architecture

### Awakening — The Second Threshold

**What It Is:** Permanent synchronization of a God Fruit's energy with its wielder's Dominion signature. Before Awakening, Fruit and user are parallel systems. After, they merge — the user doesn't just use their power better, they use it *differently*. Daeshara's Forge Fruit generates metal; Awakened, she transmutes existing metal on contact. Not a stronger version. A new ability.

**How It Happens:** Sustained extreme mastery — 8-15 years of active combat-level use creating a feedback loop between user's Dominion and Fruit energy until they synchronize permanently. No shortcuts. No rushing.

**Why It's Rare:** Most users die before reaching the threshold. One in eight ever Awaken. Ninety-four confirmed Awakened users across 5,500 years.

**The Mythical Beast Vision:** Every Mythical Beast user who Awakens sees the same thing: a grove of white-barked trees under two moons. Spiral-patterned fruit. Double shadows. The Fruit's memory of the First Age grove where it was born. The Masqarat classifies all reports of this vision. The vision proves the Eddan Trees existed. Mettavuur cannot allow that.

**Physical Cost:** Chronic fatigue, sensory distortion (Awakened Element users perceive through their element constantly), shortened peak duration, and identity bleed — after decades, the boundary between self and Fruit grows difficult to identify.

---

### God Fruit Ecology

**Total Count:** ~120-140 estimated. Masqarat registry lists 118 confirmed (Third Age onward). True number higher — Second Age records destroyed, some fruits in isolated populations, 3-4 suspected on the Sundren, and the ninth Eddan Tree may still produce new ones.

**Four Categories:**
- **Element-type** (~45-55): Direct manipulation of substance/force. Most common, most intuitive.
- **Beast-type** (~30-40): Transformation into animal forms (human, hybrid, full). Valued for versatility.
- **Law-type** (~20-25): Impose conceptual rules on reality within range. Hardest to master.
- **Mythical Beast-type** (~12-18): Folklore creatures given form. Rarest, most powerful, most dangerous to the user's identity.

**Recycling:** When a user dies, Fruit energy disperses, transits for hours to months, then reforms in a random fruit-bearing plant anywhere in the world. No predictable pattern. The hunt for newly respawned Fruits is a profession, an industry, and a cultural obsession.

**The Sundren Connection:** The ninth Eddan Tree still produces new Fruits — slowly, without Varruhn's light. These first-generation Fruits tend toward Law and Mythical Beast types, with sharper spiral patterns. The Masqarat does not know the Tree's location. Mettavuur does — it's their life-support.

---

### The Catalog — 36 Named God Fruits

*Existing 6 (profiled in Conqueror/crew sections, not cataloged below): Forge (Daeshara, Awakened), Gambit (Goltieri, Awakened), Raiju (Kuldhara, Awakened), Bull (Mavrokka Deshaan, not yet Awakened), Ledger (Caelmund Vosst), Kindling (Suuba Mettani). Additional CG fruits Measure (Ressaven Delvuun) and Boar (Kovesse Thrallek) are cataloged below.*
